         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         80–100 years
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Water_Flow_in_Semienclosed_Seaways_1-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Water_Flow_in_Semienclosed_Seaways-1">
           [1]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-bottom: #cedeff 1px solid">
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         <a href="/wiki/Category:Islands_by_body_of_water" title="Category:Islands by body of water">
          Islands
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_in_the_Mediterranean" title="List of islands in the Mediterranean">
          3300+
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         Settlements
        </th>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">
          Alexandria
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">
          Algiers
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">
          Athens
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">
          Barcelona
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">
          Beirut
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">
          Carthage
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Dubrovnik" title="Dubrovnik">
          Dubrovnik
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmir" title="İzmir">
          İzmir
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">
          Rome
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Split,_Croatia" title="Split, Croatia">
          Split
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Tangier" title="Tangier">
          Tangier
         </a>
         ,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv-Jaffa" title="Tel Aviv-Jaffa">
          Tel Aviv
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Tripoli" title="Tripoli">
          Tripoli
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">
          Tunis
         </a>
         <i>
          (
          <a href="/wiki/List_of_coastal_settlements_of_the_Mediterranean_Sea" title="List of coastal settlements of the Mediterranean Sea">
           full list
          </a>
          )
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Mediterranean Sea
       </b>
       is a
       <a href="/wiki/Sea" title="Sea">
        sea
       </a>
       connected to the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">
        Atlantic Ocean
       </a>
       , surrounded by the
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">
        Mediterranean Basin
       </a>
       and almost completely enclosed by land: on the north by
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">
        Southern Europe
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">
        Anatolia
       </a>
       , on the south by
       <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">
        North Africa
       </a>
       , and on the east by the
       <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">
        Levant
       </a>
       . Although the sea is sometimes considered a part of the Atlantic Ocean, it is usually identified as a separate body of water. Geological evidence indicates that around 5.9 million years ago, the Mediterranean was cut off from the Atlantic and was partly or completely desiccated over a period of some 600,000 years, the
       <a href="/wiki/Messinian_salinity_crisis" title="Messinian salinity crisis">
        Messinian salinity crisis
       </a>
       , before being refilled by the
       <a href="/wiki/Zanclean_flood" title="Zanclean flood">
        Zanclean flood
       </a>
       about 5.3 million years ago.
      </p>
      <p>
       The suggestion that the
       <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
        Latin
       </a>
       <i>
        mediterraneus
       </i>
       , meaning "inland" or "in the middle of land" (from
       <i>
        medius
       </i>
       , "middle" and
       <i>
        terra
       </i>
       , "land") is presumably some confusion with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo_Latin" title="Neo Latin">
        Neo Latin
       </a>
       , as within the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       , its name clearly was
       <i>
        Mare Nostrum
       </i>
       ("Our Sea")
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lowe_2002,_p.34_2-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lowe_2002,_p.34-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       . It covers an approximate area of 2.5 million km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (965,000 sq mi), but its connection to the Atlantic (the
       <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">
        Strait of Gibraltar
       </a>
       ) is only 14 km (8.7 mi) wide. The Strait of Gibraltar is a narrow strait that connects the Atlantic Ocean to the Mediterranean Sea and separates
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">
        Gibraltar
       </a>
       and Spain in Europe from
       <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
        Morocco
       </a>
       in Africa. In
       <a href="/wiki/Oceanography" title="Oceanography">
        oceanography
       </a>
       , it is sometimes called the
       <i>
        Eurafrican Mediterranean Sea
       </i>
       or the
       <i>
        European Mediterranean Sea
       </i>
       to distinguish it from
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_sea_(oceanography)" title="Mediterranean sea (oceanography)">
        mediterranean seas
       </a>
       elsewhere.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Mediterranean Sea has an average depth of 1,500 m (4,900 ft) and the deepest recorded point is 5,267 m (17,280 ft) in the
       <a href="/wiki/Calypso_Deep" title="Calypso Deep">
        Calypso Deep
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Ionian_Sea" title="Ionian Sea">
        Ionian Sea
       </a>
       . The sea is bordered on the north by
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        Europe
       </a>
       , the east by
       <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">
        Asia
       </a>
       , and in the south by
       <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">
        Africa
       </a>
       . It is located between latitudes
       <a href="/wiki/30th_parallel_north" title="30th parallel north">
        30°
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/46th_parallel_north" title="46th parallel north">
        46° N
       </a>
       and longitudes
       <a href="/wiki/6th_meridian_west" title="6th meridian west">
        6° W
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/36th_meridian_east" title="36th meridian east">
        36° E
       </a>
       . Its west-east length, from the Strait of Gibraltar to the Gulf of Iskenderun, on the southwestern coast of Turkey, is approximately 4,000 km (2,500 miles). The sea's average north-south length, from Croatia’s southern shore to Libya, is approximately 800 km (500 miles). The Mediterranean Sea, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Marmara" title="Sea of Marmara">
        Sea of Marmara
       </a>
       (connected by the
       <a href="/wiki/Dardanelles" title="Dardanelles">
        Dardanelles
       </a>
       to the
       <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">
        Aegean Sea
       </a>
       ), has a surface area of approximately 2,510,000 square km (970,000 square miles).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The sea was an important route for merchants and travellers of ancient times that allowed for trade and cultural exchange between emergent peoples of the region. The
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Mediterranean_region" title="History of the Mediterranean region">
        history of the Mediterranean region
       </a>
       is crucial to understanding the origins and development of many modern societies.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Mediterranean_countries" title="List of Mediterranean countries">
        countries with coastlines on the Mediterranean Sea
       </a>
       are
       <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">
        Albania
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">
        Algeria
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">
        Bosnia and Herzegovina
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">
        Croatia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">
        Cyprus
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
        Egypt
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
        France
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">
        Greece
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
        Israel
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">
        Italy
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">
        Lebanon
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">
        Libya
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">
        Malta
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
        Morocco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">
        Monaco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">
        Montenegro
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">
        Slovenia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
        Syria
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">
        Tunisia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">
        Turkey
       </a>
       . In addition, the
       <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">
        Gaza Strip
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">
        British Overseas Territories
       </a>
       of Gibraltar and
       <a href="/wiki/Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia" title="Akrotiri and Dhekelia">
        Akrotiri and Dhekelia
       </a>
       have coastlines on the sea.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Name">
        Name
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EFS_highres_STS034_STS034-86-96.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="2000" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/EFS_highres_STS034_STS034-86-96.jpg/220px-EFS_highres_STS034_STS034-86-96.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/EFS_highres_STS034_STS034-86-96.jpg/330px-EFS_highres_STS034_STS034-86-96.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/EFS_highres_STS034_STS034-86-96.jpg/440px-EFS_highres_STS034_STS034-86-96.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EFS_highres_STS034_STS034-86-96.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         With its highly indented coastline and large number of islands, Greece has the longest Mediterranean coastline.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The term
       <i>
        Mediterranean
       </i>
       derives from the
       <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
        Latin
       </a>
       word
       <i>
        mediterraneus
       </i>
       , meaning "amid the earth (note:
       <a href="/wiki/Soil" title="Soil">
        earth
       </a>
       in the sense "soil",
       <i>
        not
       </i>
       Planet
       <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">
        Earth
       </a>
       )" or "between land" (
       <i>
        medi-
       </i>
       ; adj.
       <i>
        medius
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        -um -a
       </i>
       "middle, between" +
       <i>
        terra
       </i>
       f., "land, earth"): as it is between the continents of
       <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">
        Africa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">
        Asia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        Europe
       </a>
       . The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_language" title="Ancient Greek language">
        Ancient Greek
       </a>
       name
       <i>
        Mesogeios
       </i>
       (Μεσόγειος), is similarly from μέσο, "between" + γη, "land, earth").
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It can be compared with the Ancient Greek name
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">
         Mesopotamia
        </a>
       </i>
       (Μεσοποταμία), meaning "between rivers".
      </p>
      <p>
       The Mediterranean Sea has historically had several names. For example, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carthaginians" title="Carthaginians">
        Carthaginians
       </a>
       called it the "Syrian Sea" and latter Romans commonly called it
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Mare_Nostrum" title="Mare Nostrum">
         Mare Nostrum
        </a>
       </i>
       ("Our Sea"), and occasionally
       <i>
        Mare Internum
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and in Greek
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title='"Romans called it" Mare Magnum "in Greek" but the term Mare Magnum is actually Latin? (January 2018)'>
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       as the "Mare Magnum", meaning "Great Sea".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-melitensia_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-melitensia-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In ancient
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syrian" title="Syrian">
        Syrian
       </a>
       texts,
       <a href="/wiki/Phoenician_language" title="Phoenician language">
        Phoenician
       </a>
       epics and in the Hebrew
       <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">
        Bible
       </a>
       , it was primarily known as the "Great Sea" (הַיָּם הַגָּדוֹל, HaYam HaGadol,
       <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Numbers" title="Book of Numbers">
        Numbers
       </a>
       34:6,7;
       <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Joshua" title="Book of Joshua">
        Joshua
       </a>
       1:4, 9:1, 15:47;
       <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Ezekiel" title="Book of Ezekiel">
        Ezekiel
       </a>
       47:10,15,20), or simply "The Sea" (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_Kings" title="1 Kings">
        1 Kings
       </a>
       5:9;
       <i>
        comp.
       </i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_Macc." title="1 Macc.">
        1 Macc.
       </a>
       14:34, 15:11); however, it has also been called the "Hinder Sea" (הַיָּם הָאַחֲרוֹן), due to its location on the west coast of
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Syria" title="Greater Syria">
        Greater Syria
       </a>
       or the
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_Land" title="Holy Land">
        Holy Land
       </a>
       , and therefore behind a person facing the east, sometimes translated as "Western Sea", (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deuteronomy" title="Deuteronomy">
        Deut.
       </a>
       11:24;
       <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Joel" title="Book of Joel">
        Joel
       </a>
       2:20). Another name was the "Sea of the
       <a href="/wiki/Philistines" title="Philistines">
        Philistines
       </a>
       " (יָם פְּלִשְׁתִּים,
       <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Exodus" title="Book of Exodus">
        Exod.
       </a>
       23:31), from the people inhabiting a large portion of its shores near the
       <a href="/wiki/Israelites" title="Israelites">
        Israelites
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">
        Modern Hebrew
       </a>
       , it has been called
       <i>
        HaYam HaTikhon
       </i>
       (הַיָּם הַתִּיכוֹן), "the Middle Sea", reflecting the Sea's name in ancient Greek (
       <i>
        Mesogeios
       </i>
       ), Latin
       <i>
        Mare internum
       </i>
       (Inner Sea) or
       <i>
        Mare Nostrum
       </i>
       (Our Sea), and modern languages in both Europe and the Middle East (
       <i>
        Mediterranean
       </i>
       , etc.).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-melitensia_8-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-melitensia-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Similarly, in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
        Modern Arabic
       </a>
       , it is known as
       <i>
        al-Baḥr [al-Abyaḍ] al-Mutawassiṭ
       </i>
       (
       <span dir="rtl">
        <span lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">
         البحر [الأبيض] المتوسط
        </span>
       </span>
       ), "the [White] Middle Sea", while in Islamic and older Arabic literature, it was referenced as
       <i>
        Baḥr al-Rūm
       </i>
       (
       <span lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">
        بحر الروم
       </span>
       ), or "the Roman/
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
        Byzantine
       </a>
       Sea."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-melitensia_8-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-melitensia-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_language" title="Ottoman Turkish language">
        Ottoman Turkish
       </a>
       , it has also been called
       <i>
        Bahr-i Sefid
       </i>
       , meaning the "Pure White Sea".
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">
        Turkish
       </a>
       , it is known as
       <i>
        Akdeniz
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       meaning "the White Sea", to distinguish it from the
       <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">
        Black Sea
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-melitensia_8-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-melitensia-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">

         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This images
          <b>
           may be
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view#Undue_weight" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">
            unbalanced
           </a>
           towards certain viewpoints
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">

      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Mediterranean_region" title="History of the Mediterranean region">
        History of the Mediterranean region
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_civilisations">
        Ancient civilisations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ancient civilisations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AntikeGriechen1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1616" data-file-width="2836" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/AntikeGriechen1.jpg/220px-AntikeGriechen1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/AntikeGriechen1.jpg/330px-AntikeGriechen1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/AntikeGriechen1.jpg/440px-AntikeGriechen1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AntikeGriechen1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Greek (red) and Phoenician (yellow)
         <a href="/wiki/Colonies_in_antiquity" title="Colonies in antiquity">
          colonies in antiquity
         </a>
         c. the 6th century BCE
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1540" data-file-width="2534" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png/220px-Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png/330px-Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png/440px-Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roman_Empire_Trajan_117AD.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
          Roman Empire
         </a>
         at its farthest extent in AD 117
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Several ancient civilisations were located around the Mediterranean shores, and were greatly influenced by their proximity to the sea. It provided routes for trade, colonisation, and war, as well as food (from fishing and the gathering of other seafood) for numerous communities throughout the ages.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Due to the shared climate, geology, and access to the sea, cultures centered on the Mediterranean tended to have some extent of intertwined culture and history.
      </p>
      <p>
       Two of the most notable Mediterranean civilisations in
       <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">
        classical antiquity
       </a>
       were the
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">
        Greek
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_state" title="City state">
        city states
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">
        Phoenicians
       </a>
       , both of which extensively colonised the coastlines of the Mediterranean. Later, when
       <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">
        Augustus
       </a>
       founded the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       , the Romans referred to the Mediterranean as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Mare_Nostrum" title="Mare Nostrum">
         Mare Nostrum
        </a>
       </i>
       ("Our Sea").
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darius_I_of_Persia" title="Darius I of Persia">
        Darius I of Persia
       </a>
       , who conquered
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">
        Ancient Egypt
       </a>
       , built a canal linking the Mediterranean to the
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">
        Red Sea
       </a>
       . Darius's canal was wide enough for two
       <a href="/wiki/Trireme" title="Trireme">
        triremes
       </a>
       to pass each other with oars extended, and required four days to traverse.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages_and_empires">
        Middle Ages and empires
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Middle Ages and empires">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1341" data-file-width="2500" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Lepanto_1571.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lepanto" title="Battle of Lepanto">
          Battle of Lepanto
         </a>
         , 1571, ended in victory for the European
         <a href="/wiki/Holy_League_(1571)" title="Holy League (1571)">
          Holy League
         </a>
         against the Ottoman Turks.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">
        Western Roman Empire
       </a>
       collapsed around AD 476. Temporarily the east was again dominant as Roman power lived on in the
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
        Byzantine Empire
       </a>
       formed in the 4th century from the eastern half of the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       . Another power arose in the 7th century, and with it the religion of
       <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
        Islam
       </a>
       , which soon swept across from the east; at its greatest extent, the
       <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">
        Arab Empire
       </a>
       controlled 75% of the Mediterranean region and left a lasting footprint on its eastern and southern shores.
      </p>
      <p>
       Europe started to revive, however, as more organised and centralised states began to form in the later
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </a>
       after the
       <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_of_the_12th_century" title="Renaissance of the 12th century">
        Renaissance of the 12th century
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven,_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2061" data-file-width="2940" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven%2C_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg/220px-thumbnail.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven%2C_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg/330px-thumbnail.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven%2C_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg/440px-thumbnail.jpeg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven,_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Bombardment_of_Algiers_(1816)" title="Bombardment of Algiers (1816)">
          bombardment of Algiers
         </a>
         by the Anglo-Dutch fleet in support of an ultimatum to release European slaves, August 1816
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman
       </a>
       power based in Anatolia continued to grow, and in 1453 extinguished the Byzantine Empire with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conquest_of_Constantinople" title="Conquest of Constantinople">
        Conquest of Constantinople
       </a>
       . Ottomans gained control of much of the sea in the 16th century and maintained naval bases in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottoman_occupation_of_Toulon" title="Ottoman occupation of Toulon">
        southern France
       </a>
       , Algeria and Tunisia.
       <a href="/wiki/Hayreddin_Barbarossa" title="Hayreddin Barbarossa">
        Barbarossa
       </a>
       , the famous Ottoman captain is a symbol of this domination with the victory of the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Preveza" title="Battle of Preveza">
        Battle of Preveza
       </a>
       (1538). The
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Djerba" title="Battle of Djerba">
        Battle of Djerba
       </a>
       (1560) marked the apex of Ottoman naval domination in the Mediterranean. As the naval prowess of the European powers increased, they confronted Ottoman expansion in the region when the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lepanto" title="Battle of Lepanto">
        Battle of Lepanto
       </a>
       (1571) checked the power of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Navy" title="Ottoman Navy">
        Ottoman Navy
       </a>
       . This was the last naval battle to be fought primarily between
       <a href="/wiki/Galley" title="Galley">
        galleys
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirates" title="Barbary pirates">
        Barbary pirates
       </a>
       of North Africa preyed on Christian shipping and coastlines in the Western Mediterranean Sea.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to Robert Davis, from the 16th to 19th centuries, pirates captured 1 million to 1.25 million Europeans as slaves.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The development of oceanic shipping began to affect the entire Mediterranean. Once, most trade between Western Europe and the East had passed through the region, but after the 1490s the development of a sea route to the Indian Ocean allowed the importation of Asian
       <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">
        spices
       </a>
       and other goods through the Atlantic ports of western Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century_and_migrations">
        21st century and migrations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 21st century and migrations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width: 272px;">
        <div class="thumbimage" style="width: 270px; height: 110px; overflow: hidden;">
         <div style="position: relative; top: -265px; left: -1055px; width: 2200px">
          <div class="noresize">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BlackMarble20161km.jpg">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="21600" data-file-width="43200" height="1100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/BlackMarble20161km.jpg/2200px-BlackMarble20161km.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/BlackMarble20161km.jpg/3300px-BlackMarble20161km.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/BlackMarble20161km.jpg/4400px-BlackMarble20161km.jpg 2x" width="2200"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:BlackMarble20161km.jpg" title="File:BlackMarble20161km.jpg">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Satellite_imagery" title="Satellite imagery">
          Satellite image
         </a>
         of the Mediterranean Sea at night
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 2013 the Maltese president described the Mediterranean sea as a "cemetery" due to the large amounts of migrants who drowned there after their boats capsized.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       European Parliament president
       <a href="/wiki/Martin_Schulz" title="Martin Schulz">
        Martin Schulz
       </a>
       said in 2014 that Europe's migration policy "turned the Mediterranean into a graveyard", referring to the number of drowned refugees in the region as a direct result of the policies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       An Azerbaijani official described the sea as "a burial ground ... where people die".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Following the
       <a href="/wiki/2013_Lampedusa_migrant_shipwreck" title="2013 Lampedusa migrant shipwreck">
        2013 Lampedusa migrant shipwreck
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Letta_Cabinet" title="Letta Cabinet">
        Italian government
       </a>
       decided to strengthen the national system for the patrolling of the Mediterranean Sea by authorising "
       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Mare_Nostrum" title="Operation Mare Nostrum">
        Operation Mare Nostrum
       </a>
       ", a military and humanitarian mission in order to rescue the migrants and arrest the traffickers of immigrants. In 2015, more than one million migrants crossed the Mediterranean Sea into Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:368px;max-width:368px">
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS059-238-074_Strait_of_Gibraltar.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="5222" data-file-width="5275" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/STS059-238-074_Strait_of_Gibraltar.jpg/180px-STS059-238-074_Strait_of_Gibraltar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/STS059-238-074_Strait_of_Gibraltar.jpg/270px-STS059-238-074_Strait_of_Gibraltar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/STS059-238-074_Strait_of_Gibraltar.jpg/360px-STS059-238-074_Strait_of_Gibraltar.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          A satellite image showing the Mediterranean Sea. The
          <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">
           Strait of Gibraltar
          </a>
          can be seen in the bottom left (north-west) quarter of the image; to its left is the
          <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">
           Iberian Peninsula
          </a>
          in
          <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
           Europe
          </a>
          , and to its right, the
          <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">
           Maghreb
          </a>
          in
          <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">
           Africa
          </a>
          .
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="653" data-file-width="653" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg/180px-Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg/270px-Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg/360px-Gallipoli_peninsula_from_space.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          The
          <a href="/wiki/Dardanelles" title="Dardanelles">
           Dardanelles
          </a>
          <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Straits" title="Turkish Straits">
           strait
          </a>
          in
          <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">
           Turkey
          </a>
          . The north side is
          <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
           Europe
          </a>
          with the
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gelibolu_Peninsula" title="Gelibolu Peninsula">
           Gelibolu Peninsula
          </a>
          in the
          <a href="/wiki/Thrace" title="Thrace">
           Thrace
          </a>
          region; the south side is
          <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">
           Anatolia
          </a>
          in
          <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">
           Asia
          </a>
          .
         </div>
        </div>
        <div style="clear:left">
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Mediterranean Sea is connected to the Atlantic Ocean by the
       <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">
        Strait of Gibraltar
       </a>
       (known in
       <a href="/wiki/Homer" title="Homer">
        Homer
       </a>
       's writings as the "
       <a href="/wiki/Pillars_of_Hercules" title="Pillars of Hercules">
        Pillars of Hercules
       </a>
       ") in the west and to the
       <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Marmara" title="Sea of Marmara">
        Sea of Marmara
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">
        Black Sea
       </a>
       , by the
       <a href="/wiki/Dardanelles" title="Dardanelles">
        Dardanelles
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosporus" title="Bosporus">
        Bosporus
       </a>
       respectively, in the east. The Sea of Marmara (
       <a href="/wiki/Dardanelles" title="Dardanelles">
        Dardanelles
       </a>
       ) is often considered a part of the Mediterranean Sea, whereas the Black Sea is generally not. The 163 km (101 mi) long artificial
       <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">
        Suez Canal
       </a>
       in the southeast connects the Mediterranean Sea to the
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">
        Red Sea
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-melitensia_8-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-melitensia-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Large islands in the Mediterranean include
       <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">
        Cyprus
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Crete" title="Crete">
        Crete
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Euboea" title="Euboea">
        Euboea
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rhodes" title="Rhodes">
        Rhodes
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lesbos_Island" title="Lesbos Island">
        Lesbos
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chios" title="Chios">
        Chios
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kefalonia" title="Kefalonia">
        Kefalonia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Corfu" title="Corfu">
        Corfu
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Limnos" title="Limnos">
        Limnos
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Samos" title="Samos">
        Samos
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naxos_Island" title="Naxos Island">
        Naxos
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Andros" title="Andros">
        Andros
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Mediterranean" title="Eastern Mediterranean">
        Eastern Mediterranean
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">
        Sicily
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cres" title="Cres">
        Cres
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Krk" title="Krk">
        Krk
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bra%C4%8D" title="Brač">
        Brač
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hvar" title="Hvar">
        Hvar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pag_(island)" title="Pag (island)">
        Pag
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kor%C4%8Dula" title="Korčula">
        Korčula
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malta_Island" title="Malta Island">
        Malta
       </a>
       in the central Mediterranean;
       <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">
        Sardinia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">
        Corsica
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">
        Balearic Islands
       </a>
       :
       <a href="/wiki/Ibiza" title="Ibiza">
        Ibiza
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Majorca" title="Majorca">
        Majorca
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Menorca" title="Menorca">
        Menorca
       </a>
       in the Western Mediterranean.
      </p>
      <p>
       The typical
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">
        Mediterranean climate
       </a>
       has hot, humid, and dry summers and mild, rainy winters. Crops of the region include
       <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">
        olives
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Grape" title="Grape">
        grapes
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Orange_(fruit)" title="Orange (fruit)">
        oranges
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tangerine" title="Tangerine">
        tangerines
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Cork_(material)" title="Cork (material)">
        cork
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Extent">
        Extent
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Extent">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/International_Hydrographic_Organization" title="International Hydrographic Organization">
        International Hydrographic Organization
       </a>
       defines the limits of the Mediterranean Sea as follows:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IHO_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-IHO-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Stretching from the
       <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">
        Strait of Gibraltar
       </a>
       in the west to the entrances to the
       <a href="/wiki/Dardanelles" title="Dardanelles">
        Dardanelles
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">
        Suez Canal
       </a>
       in the east, the Mediterranean Sea is bounded by the coasts of Europe, Africa and Asia, and is divided into two deep basins:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Western Basin:
        <ul>
         <li>
          On the west: A line joining the extremities of
          <a href="/wiki/Cape_Trafalgar" title="Cape Trafalgar">
           Cape Trafalgar
          </a>
          (Spain) and
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Spartel" title="Cape Spartel">
           Cape Spartel
          </a>
          (Africa).
         </li>
         <li>
          On the northeast: The west coast of Italy. In the
          <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Messina" title="Strait of Messina">
           Strait of Messina
          </a>
          a line joining the north extreme of Cape Paci (15°42'E) with Cape Peloro, the east extreme of the Island of
          <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">
           Sicily
          </a>
          . The north coast of Sicily.
         </li>
         <li>
          On the east: A line joining Cape Lilibeo the western point of Sicily (
          <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">
           <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;params=37_47_N_12_22_E_">
            <span class="geo-default">
             <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
              <span class="latitude">
               37°47′N
              </span>
              <span class="longitude">
               12°22′E
              </span>
             </span>
            </span>
            <span class="geo-multi-punct">
             ﻿ / ﻿
            </span>
            <span class="geo-nondefault">
             <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
              37.783°N 12.367°E
             </span>
             <span style="display:none">
              ﻿ /
              <span class="geo">
               37.783; 12.367
              </span>
             </span>
            </span>
           </a>
          </span>
          ), through the Adventure Bank to
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Bon" title="Cape Bon">
           Cape Bon
          </a>
          (Tunisia).
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        Eastern Basin:
        <ul>
         <li>
          On the west: The northeastern and eastern limits of the Western Basin.
         </li>
         <li>
          On the northeast: A line joining Kum Kale (26°11'E) and
          <a href="/wiki/Cape_Helles" title="Cape Helles">
           Cape Helles
          </a>
          , the western entrance to the Dardanelles.
         </li>
         <li>
          On the southeast: The entrance to the
          <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">
           Suez Canal
          </a>
          .
         </li>
         <li>
          On the east: The coasts of
          <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
           Syria
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
           Israel
          </a>
          .
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Oceanography">
        Oceanography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Oceanography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:367px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MEDCURR.GIF">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="250" data-file-width="497" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/MEDCURR.GIF/365px-MEDCURR.GIF" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ef/MEDCURR.GIF 1.5x" width="365"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MEDCURR.GIF" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Predominant surface currents for June
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Being nearly landlocked affects conditions in the Mediterranean Sea: for instance,
       <a href="/wiki/Tide" title="Tide">
        tides
       </a>
       are very limited as a result of the narrow connection with the Atlantic Ocean. The Mediterranean is characterised and immediately recognised by its deep blue colour.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Evaporation" title="Evaporation">
        Evaporation
       </a>
       greatly exceeds
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">
        precipitation
       </a>
       and river runoff in the Mediterranean, a fact that is central to the water circulation within the basin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Evaporation is especially high in its eastern half, causing the water level to decrease and
       <a href="/wiki/Salinity" title="Salinity">
        salinity
       </a>
       to increase eastward.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The salinity at 5 m depth is 3.8%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tempandsal_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-tempandsal-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Pressure_gradient" title="Pressure gradient">
        pressure gradient
       </a>
       pushes relatively cool, low-salinity water from the Atlantic across the basin; it warms and becomes saltier as it travels east, then sinks in the region of the
       <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">
        Levant
       </a>
       and circulates westward, to spill over the
       <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">
        Strait of Gibraltar
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Thus, seawater flow is eastward in the Strait's surface waters, and westward below; once in the Atlantic, this chemically distinct Mediterranean Intermediate Water can persist thousands of kilometres away from its source.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The temperature of the water in the deepest part of the Mediterranean Sea is 13.2 °C (55.8 °F).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tempandsal_24-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-tempandsal-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Coastal_countries">
        Coastal countries
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Coastal countries">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       For a more comprehensive list, see
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Mediterranean_countries" title="List of Mediterranean countries">
        List of Mediterranean countries
       </a>
       .
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:367px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mediterranean_Relief.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="733" data-file-width="1308" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Mediterranean_Relief.jpg/365px-Mediterranean_Relief.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Mediterranean_Relief.jpg/548px-Mediterranean_Relief.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Mediterranean_Relief.jpg/730px-Mediterranean_Relief.jpg 2x" width="365"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mediterranean_Relief.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of the Mediterranean Sea
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The following countries have a coastline on the Mediterranean Sea:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <b>
         Northern shore
        </b>
        (from west to east):
        <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
         Spain
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
         France
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">
         Monaco
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">
         Italy
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">
         Slovenia
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">
         Croatia
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">
         Bosnia and Herzegovina
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">
         Montenegro
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">
         Albania
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">
         Greece
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">
         Turkey
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Eastern shore
        </b>
        (from north to south): Turkey,
        <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
         Syria
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">
         Lebanon
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
         Israel
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Southern shore
        </b>
        (from west to east):
        <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
         Morocco
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">
         Algeria
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">
         Tunisia
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">
         Libya
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
         Egypt
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Island nations
        </b>
        :
        <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">
         Malta
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">
         Cyprus
        </a>
        .
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Several other territories also border the Mediterranean Sea (from west to east): The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_overseas_territory" title="British overseas territory">
        British overseas territory
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">
        Gibraltar
       </a>
       , the Spanish autonomous cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">
        Ceuta
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">
        Melilla
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Plazas_de_soberan%C3%ADa" title="Plazas de soberanía">
        nearby islands
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sovereign_Base_Areas" title="Sovereign Base Areas">
        Sovereign Base Areas
       </a>
       on Cyprus, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">
        Gaza Strip
       </a>
       .
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Subdivisions">
        Subdivisions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Subdivisions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="811" data-file-width="1208" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg/220px-Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg/330px-Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg/440px-Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bucht_%26_Stra%C3%9Fe_von_Gibraltar.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Africa (left, on horizon) and Europe (right), as seen from Gibraltar
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Hydrographic_Organization" title="International Hydrographic Organization">
        International Hydrographic Organization
       </a>
       (IHO), the Mediterranean Sea is subdivided into a number of smaller waterbodies, each with their own designation (from west to east):
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IHO_21-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-IHO-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">
         Strait of Gibraltar
        </a>
        ;
       </li>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Alboran_Sea" title="Alboran Sea">
         Alboran Sea
        </a>
        , between Spain and
        <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
         Morocco
        </a>
        ;
       </li>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Sea" title="Balearic Sea">
         Balearic Sea
        </a>
        , between mainland Spain and its
        <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">
         Balearic Islands
        </a>
        ;
       </li>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Ligurian_Sea" title="Ligurian Sea">
         Ligurian Sea
        </a>
        between
        <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">
         Corsica
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Liguria" title="Liguria">
         Liguria
        </a>
        (Italy);
       </li>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Tyrrhenian_Sea" title="Tyrrhenian Sea">
         Tyrrhenian Sea
        </a>
        enclosed by
        <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">
         Sardinia
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_peninsula" title="Italian peninsula">
         Italian peninsula
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">
         Sicily
        </a>
        ;
       </li>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Ionian_Sea" title="Ionian Sea">
         Ionian Sea
        </a>
        between Italy,
        <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">
         Albania
        </a>
        and Greece;
       </li>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">
         Adriatic Sea
        </a>
        between Italy,
        <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">
         Slovenia
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">
         Croatia
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">
         Bosnia and Herzegovina
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">
         Montenegro
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">
         Albania
        </a>
        ;
       </li>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">
         Aegean Sea
        </a>
        between Greece and Turkey.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_seas">
        Other seas
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Other seas">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Positano_-_01.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2591" data-file-width="3870" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Positano_-_01.jpg/220px-Positano_-_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Positano_-_01.jpg/330px-Positano_-_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Positano_-_01.jpg/440px-Positano_-_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Positano_-_01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Positano" title="Positano">
          Positano
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Tyrrhenian_Sea" title="Tyrrhenian Sea">
          Tyrrhenian Sea
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Although not recognised by the IHO treaties, there are some other seas whose names have been in common use from the ancient times, or in the present:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Sardinia" title="Sea of Sardinia">
         Sea of Sardinia
        </a>
        , between
        <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">
         Sardinia
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">
         Balearic Islands
        </a>
        , as a part of the
        <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Sea" title="Balearic Sea">
         Balearic Sea
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_of_Sicily" title="Sea of Sicily">
         Sea of Sicily
        </a>
        between
        <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">
         Sicily
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">
         Tunisia
        </a>
        ,
       </li>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Libyan_Sea" title="Libyan Sea">
         Libyan Sea
        </a>
        between
        <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">
         Libya
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Crete" title="Crete">
         Crete
        </a>
        ,
       </li>
       <li>
        In the
        <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">
         Aegean Sea
        </a>
        ,
        <ul>
         <li>
          the
          <a href="/wiki/Thracian_Sea" title="Thracian Sea">
           Thracian Sea
          </a>
          in its north,
         </li>
         <li>
          the
          <a href="/wiki/Myrtoan_Sea" title="Myrtoan Sea">
           Myrtoan Sea
          </a>
          between the
          <a href="/wiki/Cyclades" title="Cyclades">
           Cyclades
          </a>
          and the
          <a href="/wiki/Peloponnese" title="Peloponnese">
           Peloponnese
          </a>
          ,
         </li>
         <li>
          the
          <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Crete" title="Sea of Crete">
           Sea of Crete
          </a>
          north of Crete,
         </li>
         <li>
          the
          <a href="/wiki/Icarian_Sea" title="Icarian Sea">
           Icarian Sea
          </a>
          between
          <a href="/wiki/Kos" title="Kos">
           Kos
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Chios" title="Chios">
           Chios
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cilician_Sea" title="Cilician Sea">
         Cilician Sea
        </a>
        between Turkey and
        <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">
         Cyprus
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Levantine_Sea" title="Levantine Sea">
         Levantine Sea
        </a>
        at the eastern end of the Mediterranean
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Many of these smaller seas feature in local myth and folklore and derive their names from these associations.
      </p>

      <p>
       In addition to the seas, a number of
       <a href="/wiki/Headlands_and_bays" title="Headlands and bays">
        gulfs
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Strait" title="Strait">
        straits
       </a>
       are also recognised:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Saint_George_Bay" title="Saint George Bay">
         Saint George Bay
        </a>
        in Beirut, Lebanon
       </li>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Ras_Ibn_Hani" title="Ras Ibn Hani">
         Ras Ibn Hani
        </a>
        cape in
        <a href="/wiki/Latakia" title="Latakia">
         Latakia
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
         Syria
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Ras_al-Bassit" title="Ras al-Bassit">
         Ras al-Bassit
        </a>
        cape in northern Syria.
       </li>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Minet_el-Beida" title="Minet el-Beida">
         Minet el-Beida
        </a>
        ("White Harbour") bay near ancient
        <a href="/wiki/Ugarit" title="Ugarit">
         Ugarit
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
         Syria
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">
         Strait of Gibraltar
        </a>
        , connects the Atlantic Ocean to the Mediterranean Sea and separates Spain from
        <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
         Morocco
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Gibraltar" title="Bay of Gibraltar">

        </a>

        <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">
         Iberian Peninsula
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Corinth" title="Gulf of Corinth">
         Gulf of Corinth
        </a>

        <a href="/wiki/Corinth_Canal" title="Corinth Canal">
         Corinth Canal
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Pagasetic_Gulf" title="Pagasetic Gulf">

        </a>

        </a>

        </a>

         peninsula
        </a>

        </a>

         Mirtoan Sea
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Thermaic_Gulf" title="Thermaic Gulf">

        </a>

        <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">

        </a>

        </a>

        </a>
        , southern Italy

          </a>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediterranean_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb noresize tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:777px;">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="">
        <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koppen_World_Map_(Mediterranean_Sea_area_only).png" title="Map of climate zones in the areas surrounding the Mediterranean Sea, according to the Köppen climate classification">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="260" data-file-width="769" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f8/Koppen_World_Map_%28Mediterranean_Sea_area_only%29.png" width="769"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen_World_Map_(Mediterranean_Sea_area_only).png" title="File:Koppen World Map (Mediterranean Sea area only).png">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of climate zones in the areas surrounding the Mediterranean Sea, according to the
         <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">

         </a>
        </div>

      </div>
